<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_4ebdcff3-5ae0-40b9-84b8-a68216e7a1fb'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/286388-this-book-sounds-really-interesting-and-i">This book sounds really interesting, and I was very excited to read it until I noticed that one of its genres is horror, and I like to sleep at night, thank you very much.
So I wanted to ask, is this book scary? is it terrifying? can a person that considers books marked as thriller scary read this?</a>
</div>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I'm reading it now. It definitely has a haunting and chilling feel to it, but I wouldn't call it horror, exactly. It's kind of Grimm's Fairy Tale scar<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I'm reading it now. It definitely has a haunting and chilling feel to it, but I wouldn't call it horror, exactly. It's kind of Grimm's Fairy Tale scary, rather than Stephen King scary. Has a very folkloric feel about it.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/1814023-jessica"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1231301890i/1814023.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/1814023-jessica">Jessica</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I think it was from the war in the 3rd story, when the planes flew over the island and dropped their bombs 'to be lighter, so they could fly faster' b<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I think it was from the war in the 3rd story, when the planes flew over the island and dropped their bombs 'to be lighter, so they could fly faster' but ending up killing Sarah, the daughter of the couple that was taking care of the injured airman. I figured it was from that. Just another way to connect the stories, without being as significant as some of the other connections.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer230962390" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13900017635342719785">Why are readers drawn to horror? Read our <a href='http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2013/02/q-with-midwinterblood-author-marcus.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Q & A with Marcus Sedgwick</a>, the Printz honor author of Midwinterblood. Plus win a finished copy of this fantastic book!<br/><br/><b>4.5 stars</b> <b>
  <i>Blood-soaked nightmares. Of another time. Of another place. Of another life.</i>
</b><br/><br/>The unusual story of <i>Midwinterblood</i> begins in the future, in the year 2073. A young journalist named Eric arrives on a remote island, where it is rumored that the people live forever. He is immediately drawn to a woman named Merle, but soon begins t</span>
  <span id="freeText13900017635342719785" style="display:none">Why are readers drawn to horror? Read our <a href="http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2013/02/q-with-midwinterblood-author-marcus.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Q &amp; A with Marcus Sedgwick</a>, the Printz honor author of Midwinterblood. Plus win a finished copy of this fantastic book!<br /><br /><b>4.5 stars</b> <b>
  <i>Blood-soaked nightmares. Of another time. Of another place. Of another life.</i>
</b><br /><br />The unusual story of <i>Midwinterblood</i> begins in the future, in the year 2073. A young journalist named Eric arrives on a remote island, where it is rumored that the people live forever. He is immediately drawn to a woman named Merle, but soon begins to notice that the locals are behaving strangely...very strangely. Little does he know that his story is but one chapter in a piercingly poignant, savage saga that stretches across time and transcends the boundaries of life and death.<br /><br />I love fiction that is unsettling, particularly when it comes to the YA genre. Eric and Merle's story has elements of the shrieking madness of the film <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0070917/" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wicker Man</a>, including a distinct undercurrent of unease and disturbing pagan rituals. To tell you too much about the seven interconnected stories would be to give away too many of their delicious secrets. But following the opening segment, the plot moves backwards in time, and by the third story "The Airman," the pieces start fitting together. My favorite ones are "The Painter"(1902), "The Unquiet Grave" (1848), and "The Vampire" (10th Century), many of which are violent, pensive, and sad. One of the things I like best about the plot is how Eric and Merle are bound together throughout the centuries, and yet their relationship is never the same. Sometimes they are lovers, sometimes they are children, etc., but there is always a connective emotional thread between them.<br /><br />The prose is descriptive and powerful, with fragments of rough beauty jutting out from the horror contained in the intricate framework of the story. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Behind them grew a tree, an odd tree, with a straight trunk, and a pointed crown of brilliant green leaves. Gold objects hung in the glossy leaves, and Bridget was startled as she saw they were skulls. Shining golden skulls.</i>
</b><br /><br />Although I read a great many books for sheer entertainment value, it's coming across an author like Marcus Sedgwick that reminds me how very formulaic many YA books tend to be. When I read his chilling gothic mystery <i>White Crow</i> last year, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/213197711" rel="nofollow noopener">it freaked me out</a>--I couldn't believe the intensity of the emotional pitch, or how the persuasively suggestive writing played tricks with my perception. <i>Midwinterblood</i> solidified the author's place on my list of favorite writers, and I will be seeking out every title of his that I can get my hands on. I wish we saw more YA with this degree of depth and complexity.<br /><br />If you're the type of reader who prefers goth over gore, mood over mayhem, or disquiet over digust, this is exactly the kind of horror story that will appeal to you--one that is odd and beautifully strange, and one written with passion, but also with great restraint. Unapologetically bold, horrifying, and desperately doomed, <i>Midwinterblood</i> is not a book any reader could easily forget. <br /><br /><b>Recommended for:</b> fans of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12971662.Monstrous_Beauty" title="Monstrous Beauty by Elizabeth Fama" rel="nofollow noopener">Monstrous Beauty</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11388429.When_the_Sea_is_Rising_Red" title="When the Sea is Rising Red by Cat Hellisen" rel="nofollow noopener">When the Sea is Rising Red</a>, and other dark literary YA, and for adults who may want to try out some quality young adult fiction. Also recommended for fans of the time-crossing elements of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/49628.Cloud_Atlas" title="Cloud Atlas by David Mitchell" rel="nofollow noopener">Cloud Atlas</a>, as well as the crazy fun of <i>The Wicker Man.</i> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Although this is much less phallically obsessed, hee hee. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><i>This review also appears in <a href="http://www.themidnightgarden.net/2013/01/midwinterblood-review.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Midnight Garden</a>. An advance copy was provided by the publisher.</i><br /><br /><b>Midwinterblood Tour Stop</b><br /><br />We're very pleased to be kicking off the official Midwinterblood Blog Tour next <b>Monday, February 5th</b>! Stop by for our Q &amp; A with author Marcus Sedgwick, when you may also enter to win a copy of this spectacular book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13900017635342719785" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1924035173" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1924035173?book_show_action=true">Jul 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781250040077" href="/book/show/17978165-midwinterblood">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">suspense or magical realism fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2017">z-read2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=nonfiction">nonfiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=author-love">author-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=5-star">5-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-relationships">favorite-relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-faves2017">z-faves2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2000">y-out2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=gay-genre-fiction">gay-genre-fiction</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1924035173" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1983589593741063231">For some reason I considered giving this four stars, but honestly, why should I? I read <i>Midwinterblood</i> in one sitting, I still can't think of a single thing I didn't like, and it kind of changed my life. This deserves a full five and a place on my favorites list. <br/><br/><b>Marcus Sedgwick is such an odd writer.</b> His books don't quite have a genre. Are they sci-fi? Are they magical realism? Are they suspense? Maybe. Partially. But those genre labels don't come close to describing his books. The only other b</span>
  <span id="freeText1983589593741063231" style="display:none">For some reason I considered giving this four stars, but honestly, why should I? I read <i>Midwinterblood</i> in one sitting, I still can't think of a single thing I didn't like, and it kind of changed my life. This deserves a full five and a place on my favorites list. <br /><br /><b>Marcus Sedgwick is such an odd writer.</b> His books don't quite have a genre. Are they sci-fi? Are they magical realism? Are they suspense? Maybe. Partially. But those genre labels don't come close to describing his books. The only other book I can even compare to the two of his books that I've read might be <i>Where Futures End</i> by Parker Peevyhouse, another one that I loved. I feel like I need to establish a new genre for his works alone. I can't recommend this to you by genre; I can only say <b>“read this if you like books where you won't fully get it until the end and you don't see anything coming”.</b><br /><br />One thing is certain— <b>Sedgwick has a talent for dramatic tension</b> This book was just so twisty and fascinating that I couldn't put it down. And not only could I not put it down, I felt so engaged constantly. <b>I even had visceral reactions to all the twists</b>. For example, there's a bit right at the end of part four that kind of changed me as a person?? Just... the symbolism. I legitimately had to take a few deep breaths because I felt so fucked up. It was really unsettling. There's a line at the end of section six that also fucked me up. I don't know why I didn't see it coming, but I didn't at all and I almost choked when I read it. <br /><br />This book made me pretty <b>emotional</b> too. The end of part five actually made me cry a little. I just... I didn't see it coming, but it changed me. I am <i>shooketh</i>. I don't even particularly know why - the characters are fine, but nothing very special. It was the humanity and eerie nature of this story that I loved so much. <br /><br />And again, I can't spoil what made me emotional. I can't spoil what made me happy and unhappy. I was just so, so engaged in all of this. <b>All I can say is please put this on your tbr.</b> Please. <br /><br /><a href="http://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/52545435-elise-the-bookish-actress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a>| <a href="https://twitter.com/kaz_inej" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCVIY_GxZIuclzsIw9CLSe3g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer207658707" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8746376737684384024"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>What a pleasant surprise this book was. It's the first one I've read by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/110234.Marcus_Sedgwick' title='Marcus Sedgwick' rel='nofollow noopener'>Marcus Sedgwick</a>, I've been putting off reading his other works after hearing them repeatedly described as "weird". And I get that, this was extremely weird and the kind of book that makes very little sense until the end. But it was a great story, the writing was brilliant and I really liked the whole concept.<br/><br/>This is a very difficult review to write beyond using rather empty adjectives like "amazing" and "great", mostly b</span>
  <span id="freeText8746376737684384024" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>What a pleasant surprise this book was. It's the first one I've read by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/110234.Marcus_Sedgwick" title="Marcus Sedgwick" rel="nofollow noopener">Marcus Sedgwick</a>, I've been putting off reading his other works after hearing them repeatedly described as "weird". And I get that, this was extremely weird and the kind of book that makes very little sense until the end. But it was a great story, the writing was brilliant and I really liked the whole concept.<br><br>This is a very difficult review to write beyond using rather empty adjectives like "amazing" and "great", mostly because it was so odd. What can I write without giving something important away? I will say that this has made my mind up about needing to read the author's other books, I already have <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6491917.Revolver" title="Revolver by Marcus Sedgwick" rel="nofollow noopener">Revolver</a> sitting on my shelf and I plan on getting to it as soon as possible.<br><br>The actual idea behind this story is one that has been explored many times but the way in which it is done here is highly original (and slightly mind-boggling). I can understand why Sedgwick's books are not very widely read, especially seeing as he is writing for a teenage audience. In my local library, his books aren't even in the teen section, but on the 8-12 shelves. There's very little chance that younger readers will care for his writing even if they do manage to understand it. Perhaps both he and his publisher need to rethink the target audience?<br><br><i>Many thanks to UK Book Tours for sending me this ARC.</i><br></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1089014461" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1089014461" />
    <a title="Ferdy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy"><img alt="Ferdy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487898103p2/4596358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1089014461?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ferdy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ferdy" href="/user/show/4596358-ferdy">Ferdy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781596438026" href="/book/show/15794941-midwinterblood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=wtf">wtf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=wtfery">wtfery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4596358-ferdy?shelf=weird">weird</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1089014461" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6120507496384399743"><b>Spoilers</b><br/><br/>This was a bit of an unusual YA novel, there was nothing really YA about it (except maybe the insta-love). <br/>The premise and the mystery of sorts was quite engrossing until the actual 'reveal' at the end, which was a let down. The characters, the relationships, the worldbuilding and the ending weren't that great either.<br/><br/>-What's what: The seven lives of Eric, Merle and their so called love. Each reincarnation has a different short story of sorts and are all set on the mysterious Blessed isla</span>
  <span id="freeText6120507496384399743" style="display:none"><b>Spoilers</b><br /><br />This was a bit of an unusual YA novel, there was nothing really YA about it (except maybe the insta-love). <br />The premise and the mystery of sorts was quite engrossing until the actual 'reveal' at the end, which was a let down. The characters, the relationships, the worldbuilding and the ending weren't that great either.<br /><br />-What's what: The seven lives of Eric, Merle and their so called love. Each reincarnation has a different short story of sorts and are all set on the mysterious Blessed island. <br />The first story set in 2073 focuses on journalist Eric, who visits the island to investigate the rumours surrounding it. Once there he feels a connection with Merle, then weird things happen and the stories about their past reincarnations are told. <br /><br />-This didn't seem like a YA book, nothing about it felt like YA. None of the main characters were teenagers or younger, and there were no themes that were YA centred. There was nothing about school/education, family, identity, friendship, first relationships, the future etc. <br />It didn't read like an adult novel either as the writing was too simplistic. It was a rather random mystery about two characters who fell in insta-love and that was it. There was no character or relationship development, there were no struggles or issues or themes or messages. It was quite an odd read.<br /><br />-Was I supposed to be rooting for Eric and Merle? They barely even interacted in the first story, their relationship was non-existent. And the other stories of their past selves put me off their romance completely. They started off as husband and wife, but they were later also mother and son, siblings, and old man/young neighbour girl - after that it felt creepy for them to be attracted to each other in their present lives. I was left thinking why supposed soulmates would be reincarnated as siblings and mother and son? Why, just why?<br /><br />-I was more interested in the mysteries of the island and its secretive inhabitants than the love story between the two MC's. I wanted to know what was going on on the island. Why was the dragon flower only on one half of the island? Why was it hidden when everyone on the island used it? Why did Tor and everyone else think sacrificing Eric would mean they could have kids again? It wasn't like they were living in the olden days where they believed in sacrifice and whatnot. If the islanders wanted kids so badly why didn't they stop using the plant which made them barren? Did other versions of Merle/Eric remember their past selves? Why did Eric suddenly remember everything at the end? Was Tor reincarnated too? Did he remember his past life? Why was the island so isolated, secretive and separate from the rest of the world? What was with the hares? Why was there little modern technology on the island? How was it that Merle died in 2002 in <i>The Airman</i> story yet in 2011 she was a middle aged woman with a teenage son? How could one plant have such a variety of uses? The dragon flower was used for sleeping, healing, killing, prolonged age and forgetfulness. How could it be the main ingredient for such different things? The 2011 Eric knew where the past Viking version of himself was buried, he also knew the life he had wasn't his last one.. So he remembered his other lives, did he not then find it weird that his mum was his lover/wife in the past? Did his mum remember their other lives? If not, why? Why didn't other past Eric's/Merle's ever remember? Did 2011 Eric only remember because he had brain damage? What was with the random ghost telling the story to the kids? What was with the random vampire?<br />I was expecting a lot more answers by the end, very little was explained, it was like we were meant to accept things because that's just the way it was. I wanted proper answers and proper worldbuilding. <br /><br />-The whole centuries long 'love' story of Eric/Merle started because the first Eric from back in the day was a king who willingly sacrificed himself to the gods so his island/people would be fertile. Anyway, when he was dying he promised to live seven lives in total (why not eight or nine or twenty?), and he asked his wife to follow him. He said he would look for her in each life so he could love her and they could be together. The queen went crazy after his death and then disappeared for years, and when she reappeared she basically shrugged and said she would follow him. I don't know how or why them simply saying they would be reincarnated again and again actually made it possible. Anyway, the other lives/stories have them reuniting or sort of reuniting but never actually being together. So yea, their reincarnations ended up being a bit of a damp squib.<br /><br />-The love story between Eric/Merle should have been epic considering it started centuries ago and they promised to be together in each of their next six lives because they just loved each other that much. Instead in most of their other lives there love was either weird, non-existent or meh, which made their love story even more unconvincing and daft. It didn't help that the Eric in the first story didn't even seem to love Merle much. He was all <i>'from all three of my wives, she's been my favourite, she's a pretty cool lady'.</i> And then when he was dying he was suddenly <i>'ooh, I'm going promise to live more lives so I can be with my fave wife again, also me saying that we'll be together again will ensure my supposed beloved wife will never move on from me, also I want my last words to be dramatic'.</i> It was hard to find their 'love' romantic or tragic when pretty much all the feelings involved were shallow and unbelievable.<br /><br />-The first story in 2073 (their seventh/last life) with the journalist visiting the island and falling in insta-love with Merle ended with both of them being sacrificed. Which made all their lives pointless, the whole point of their reincarnation was so they could be together again, they never got to be together properly in any of their lives. And since their seventh life was meant to be their last they would never be together again, so all those lives were kind of pointless. <br /><br />-In <i>The Archaeologist</i> story Merle/Eric were mother and son, it was weird and cringey. Also, the parent/child love they had was utterly mundane, Merle seemed mostly annoyed by Eric. <br /><br />-In <i>The Airman</i> they didn't even meet, Eric was married to some other woman he loved (so much for his everlasting love for Merle!) and Merle was child in a different country. Eric saving Merle's father wasn't them being together or loving each other, so that was another story which made Eric/Merle's centuries 'love' more ridiculous than tragic. <br /><br />-In the <i>The Painter</i>, Eric was an old artist and Merle was a child/his neighbour, they didn't love each other, they just had a little bit of a granddad/granddaughter relationship for a few months. Eric cared far more about his painting/art than Merle and Merle cared more about the apples she found. Not that I wanted any romantic love between the two, but if I was meant to believe in them being soulmates and tragic lovers who were torn apart then there should have been a profound connection between the two, not just a grumpy neighbour getting to know his neighbours.<br /><br />-In <i>The Unquiet Grave</i> Eric was Erica and she fell in love with Merle, which was forbidden since they were both women. The love Erica/Merle had in this one was the most convincing and epic. The other stories paled in comparison and made Eric/Merle seem like two twits who were never actually in love.<br /><br />-In <i>The Vampire</i> they were twins, I expected them to have a strong bond that no-one could break or compete against but instead they were normal siblings. Eric was more interested in his dad and Merle wasn't even all that bothered about Eric.<br /><br />-The various stories didn't make Eric/Merle tragic or epic or meant-to-be, if anything I was convinced there was nothing profound or deep about them. They were just two dramatic fools who made silly promises to each other and their reincarnations proved there was nothing much between them, and that they could more than live fulfilled/happy lives without one another.<br /><br />All in all, I wasn't impressed with this. Even though the idea of reincarnation and epic love has been done to death, I was still intrigued by it. Sadly, the execution of it all was a let down. It was just a weird story.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6120507496384399743" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1333059621?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vanessa J." class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vanessa J." href="/user/show/19590155-vanessa-j">Vanessa J.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=mindfuck">mindfuck</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19590155-vanessa-j?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1333059621" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11084358961868987222"><b>4.5 out of 5 stars</b><br/><br/>See this?<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437358735i/15577587._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I changed my bio on <a href='https://bookswithchemistry.wordpress.com' rel='nofollow noopener'>my blog</a> to include Marcus Sedgwick amongst my favourite authors. After reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21469108.The_Ghosts_of_Heaven' title='The Ghosts of Heaven by Marcus Sedgwick' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Ghosts of Heaven</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896184.White_Crow' title='White Crow by Marcus Sedgwick' rel='nofollow noopener'>White Crow</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10836471.Midwinterblood' title='Midwinterblood by Marcus Sedgwick' rel='nofollow noopener'>Midwinterblood</a>, I finally realised he belongs there.<br/><br/>What is <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10836471.Midwinterblood' title='Midwinterblood by Marcus Sedgwick' rel='nofollow noopener'>Midwinterblood</a>? It's a story about two souls, told in seven parts. It starts in the year 2073 with the journalist Eric Seven arriving on the island Blessed, in which there are strange rumours about the people. When he gets there, he meets a beautiful woman called Merle and som</span>
  <span id="freeText11084358961868987222" style="display:none"><b>4.5 out of 5 stars</b><br><br>See this?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1437358735i/15577587._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I changed my bio on <a href="https://bookswithchemistry.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">my blog</a> to include Marcus Sedgwick amongst my favourite authors. After reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21469108.The_Ghosts_of_Heaven" title="The Ghosts of Heaven by Marcus Sedgwick" rel="nofollow noopener">The Ghosts of Heaven</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896184.White_Crow" title="White Crow by Marcus Sedgwick" rel="nofollow noopener">White Crow</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10836471.Midwinterblood" title="Midwinterblood by Marcus Sedgwick" rel="nofollow noopener">Midwinterblood</a>, I finally realised he belongs there.<br><br>What is <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10836471.Midwinterblood" title="Midwinterblood by Marcus Sedgwick" rel="nofollow noopener">Midwinterblood</a>? It's a story about two souls, told in seven parts. It starts in the year 2073 with the journalist Eric Seven arriving on the island Blessed, in which there are strange rumours about the people. When he gets there, he meets a beautiful woman called Merle and something clicks in him.<br><br>You've surely felt those déjà vu moments, don't you? Well, this is what happens to Eric: He feels as if he has met Merle before, but he can't recall where he saw her.<br><br>However, before he finally gets his answer, the people on the isle decide to sacrifice him. And so starts the book.<br><br>I've got to say I love Sedgwick's writing. It's so... sublime. For every author on my favourites list, I have a word to describe their writing style. For Leah Raeder, for example, that word is explosive. For Marcus Sedgwick, the word I've chosen is <b>sublime</b>. It transports me to another word, and it drugs me.<br><br>That sounds dramatic, doesn't it? Well, say what you will, but that's how I feel. Thing is, he has a way to deliver words that make you get instantly hooked in the story and the labyrinth that's beneath it (because they can get hard to understand sometimes, or they can play with your mind), and I'm not saying this lightly.<br><br>I don't want to spoil too much about the story, but just know that it is really captivating. It starts in the year 2073, and it goes backwards from there. The more you read, the more you're going to understand the complexity behind what the synopsis says.<br><br>Some people describe Marcus Sedgwick's books as weird. I don't agree with them. Yes, they're really different to most YA books, but that's what makes them special. Maybe people say they're weird because his books don't have any of the content present in most of the popular YA books. I don't know, and I really don't care. What matters is that I love them.<br><br>Reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10836471.Midwinterblood" title="Midwinterblood by Marcus Sedgwick" rel="nofollow noopener">Midwinterblood</a> only confirmed what I already accepted as a fact: Marcus Sedgwick is a genius. I'd love to know how his head works. My expectations for anything by Sedgwick are now beyond high. That's a risk when reading books, but I really doubt he will disappoint.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11084358961868987222" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Neil (or bleed)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14057379-neil-or-bleed"><img alt="Neil (or bleed)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572821192p2/14057379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/835958512?book_show_action=true">Jan 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Neil (or bleed)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Neil (or bleed)" href="/user/show/14057379-neil-or-bleed">Neil (or bleed)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14057379-neil-or-bleed?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14057379-neil-or-bleed?shelf=books-from-my-favorite-authors">books-from-my-favorite-authors</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14057379-neil-or-bleed?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer835958512" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8181047180675436886">EDIT: I found a copy of Midwinterblood in Booksale.<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458100392i/18443670.jpg' width='240' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>But I can't find this cover/edition on Goodreads. Shame.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>"To bless means to sacrifice, and in blood."</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>The first time I learned about Midwinterblood is when I've read a post about Printz-honor books of 2014. Midwinterblood is one of the short-listed. In the end, it won the prestigious Michael L. Printz Award. But I didn't read the book at that time since I thought I will not enjoy this book. And that's one of the worst mistake I made in my life</span>
  <span id="freeText8181047180675436886" style="display:none">EDIT: I found a copy of Midwinterblood in Booksale.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458100392i/18443670.jpg" width="240" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>But I can't find this cover/edition on Goodreads. Shame.<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"To bless means to sacrifice, and in blood."</i>
</blockquote><br><br>The first time I learned about Midwinterblood is when I've read a post about Printz-honor books of 2014. Midwinterblood is one of the short-listed. In the end, it won the prestigious Michael L. Printz Award. But I didn't read the book at that time since I thought I will not enjoy this book. And that's one of the worst mistake I made in my life because now that I've read all I can say is I LOVED it!<br><br>Midwinterblood is one of the books that "if you know less before reading it, the better". I had the experience for that. I started this book without much knowledge what it is all about and I'm glad for it since I had really appreciated the book's beauty and brilliance. So, to be fair, I won't say much (because frankly, I really don't know what to say lol).<br><br>Midwinterblood is an epic tale of love and memories that transcends time. It is a compelling and page-turner. It is unique and original. It is odd and weird. I don't exactly know what is happening in the first chapter but it made me curious as fuck. Which is an enough reason to push through and boy, it was all worth it. Chapter by chapter, it builds up my anticipation and that gut feeling inside my chest. That feeling which, somehow, I already knew what I am reading and at the same time, I don't. I swear, Marcus Sedgwick is a hella good of a writer for doing this to me. <br><br>If you already read his books, you know, he didn't write a typical YA novel and that's what I liked about him. Midwinterblood is not an exemption. So, yeah, READ IT! :D<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="8181047180675436886" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

Now don't knock this book down. If you haven't read any <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/110234.Marcus_Sedgwick' title='Marcus Sedgwick' rel='nofollow noopener'>Marcus Sedgwick</a>, then it's time you should.<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10836471.Midwinterblood' title='Midwinterblood by Marcus Sedgwick' rel='nofollow noopener'>Midwinterblood</a> is one of the weirdest book that I read.</b><br/><br/><br/>Here's a tip:<b>
  <u> You have to finish the book. </u>
</b><br/><br/> Some people find it difficult to finish the book because it's weird. Well, poptarts are weird but still, you eat it because it's for your own good. Same with this book, all the weirdness connects and after the last page of the book</span>
  <span id="freeText7134238156291806589" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446496363i/16817457._SY540_.png" width="500" height="600" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>This book has a Viking, Vampires, Ghosts and very powerful orchid. Now don't knock this book down. If you haven't read any <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/110234.Marcus_Sedgwick" title="Marcus Sedgwick" rel="nofollow noopener">Marcus Sedgwick</a>, then it's time you should.<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10836471.Midwinterblood" title="Midwinterblood by Marcus Sedgwick" rel="nofollow noopener">Midwinterblood</a> is one of the weirdest book that I read.</b><br><br><br>Here's a tip:<b>
  <u> You have to finish the book. </u>
</b><br><br> Some people find it difficult to finish the book because it's weird. Well, poptarts are weird but still, you eat it because it's for your own good. Same with this book, all the weirdness connects and after the last page of the book, you'll find yourself in dazed and you'll say <i> "I need a moment.."</i><br><br>The first few chapters of the book really scared me. Because who thought deja vu is deliciously creepy?Then the story began to unfold and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/110234.Marcus_Sedgwick" title="Marcus Sedgwick" rel="nofollow noopener">Marcus Sedgwick</a> swept you away with a love story that defies time and logic.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1446496364i/16817458.jpg" width="540" height="304" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br>I have a habit of reading weird stories and I appreciate them, so if you want a different kind of story that doesn't have any cliche on it, then go please check out <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10836471.Midwinterblood" title="Midwinterblood by Marcus Sedgwick" rel="nofollow noopener">Midwinterblood</a>. It'll blow your mind.<br></span>

<div id="review_1026464158" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1026464158" />
    <a title="Chantal " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31668723-chantal"><img alt="Chantal " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464626501p2/31668723.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1026464158?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chantal " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chantal " href="/user/show/31668723-chantal">Chantal </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chantal  by: </span>
      Vane
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31668723-chantal?shelf=listened-on-audio">listened-on-audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1026464158" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer880234897271741369"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>I finished this book more than a week ago and I still don’t know how to review or rate it. How do you review a novel like this? <b>The story is so much stranger and so different from other things I’ve read that it’s difficult to compare.</b> What I do know though is that I really enjoyed it. It only took about a page before I was sucked into the story; the novel is very intriguing and <b>once you start you won’t want to put it down</b>. <br/><br/>I’m not going to tell you what <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10836471.Midwinterblood' title='Midwinterblood by Marcus Sedgwick' rel='nofollow noopener'>Midwinterblood</a> is about because I</span>
  <span id="freeText880234897271741369" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />I finished this book more than a week ago and I still don’t know how to review or rate it. How do you review a novel like this? <b>The story is so much stranger and so different from other things I’ve read that it’s difficult to compare.</b> What I do know though is that I really enjoyed it. It only took about a page before I was sucked into the story; the novel is very intriguing and <b>once you start you won’t want to put it down</b>. <br /><br />I’m not going to tell you what <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10836471.Midwinterblood" title="Midwinterblood by Marcus Sedgwick" rel="nofollow noopener">Midwinterblood</a> is about because I think it’s a book you should go into blind. All I will say is that it consists of different story threads – almost like separate short stories – that all tie together in the end. <br /><br /><u>Here are the reasons why I enjoyed <i>Mindwinterblood</i>:</u><br /><br />-	<b>The writing</b>: This is my first <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/110234.Marcus_Sedgwick" title="Marcus Sedgwick" rel="nofollow noopener">Marcus Sedgwick</a> book but it definitely won’t be my last. His writing style is fantastic: it’s beautiful yet simple and pulls you into the story immediately. Sedgwick has this ability to create atmosphere in only a few sentences where other authors need paragraphs upon paragraphs (if they manage it at all). His writing transports you; I felt like I was right there, living life on Blessed Island, drinking the tea, smelling the flowers. For me, the writing was the strongest aspect of the novel.<br />-	<b>Reading this novel felt a bit like taking a vacation.</b> It was as if I was living in another world, everything else fell away. I don’t know if that was because of the writing style, the setting or both but I felt really relaxed after I had finished. <br />-	<b>An old, overused concept was made new.</b> I won’t get into details because of spoilers but this book basically takes a story that has been done over and over again and manages to make it feel totally fresh and different. It didn’t feel like a rehash, it didn’t feel like something I had read before. Usually, my biggest problem with this particular storyline is that it often feels somewhat…cheap, but <i>Midwinterblood</i> was the opposite, it was intricate and beautiful. <br />-	<b>The story felt both timeless and ageless.</b> This book is marketed as YA but honestly, I’m not sure why. I think adults would enjoy this book just as much as teens if not more. <br /><br /><u>What didn’t work for me:</u><br /><br />I’m struggling to put my finger on it but I think there was just <b>something missing</b> for me. For one thing, <b>I didn’t connect with any of the characters</b>. There was barely any characterisation. Now, that sounds a lot worse than it actually is: this story isn’t really about attachment to the characters but much more plot and theme driven. However, it is at its core a love story and unfortunately I couldn’t really root for the lovers. <b>I felt very detached.</b> <br /><br />My other and main problem was the ending. <b>It didn’t satisfy me.</b> I had SO many questions and none of them were answered. This book is very intriguing and interesting and I JUST WANTED TO KNOW WHAT WAS GOING ON. Ultimately though, the ending didn’t give me anything that I hadn’t already guessed. Things weren’t properly explained and maybe (probably) that wasn’t the point of the story but it still made me sad. When I’m so invested in a book it’s difficult for me to just accept things without questioning. <br /><br /><b><i>Midwinterblood</i> is an engaging book that is excellently written but won’t be to everyone’s taste. I recommend it to those readers, who want something different, something a little strange.</b> <br /><br />As for me, I can’t wait to pick up another book by <i>Marcus Sedgwick</i>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="880234897271741369" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_622280177" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/622280177" />
    <a title="Beth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4063913-beth"><img alt="Beth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351396026p2/4063913.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/622280177?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beth" href="/user/show/4063913-beth">Beth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781596438002" href="/book/show/15792870-midwinterblood">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4063913-beth?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer622280177" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3566140810632558573">After telling people all week that I don't understand how Newbery and Printz criteria actually lead to objectivity, I'm going to try to review this book objectively as an exercise. <br/><br/>1. Is there a plot arc? No. There is no plot. This is a character-focused work.<br/><br/>2. Is there a character arc? Surprisingly, no. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[This is the story of the way Eric sacrifices himself for six generations until Merle sacrifices herself with him the seventh time, which is supposedly evidence of great love. Tha</span></span>
  <span id="freeText3566140810632558573" style="display:none">After telling people all week that I don't understand how Newbery and Printz criteria actually lead to objectivity, I'm going to try to review this book objectively as an exercise. <br /><br />1. Is there a plot arc? No. There is no plot. This is a character-focused work.<br /><br />2. Is there a character arc? Surprisingly, no. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This is the story of the way Eric sacrifices himself for six generations until Merle sacrifices herself with him the seventh time, which is supposedly evidence of great love. That is not character growth. That is a profoundly disturbing replacement for character growth. <br /><br />The one interesting thing is the way Eric and Merle's relationship changes in each generation, but this is something that weakens the book, too. (When Eric is a painter, for example, and Merle is his neighbor, and he dies of grief after his painting is rejected by a museum, that death is positioned as his sacrifice. That's not a sacrifice.) And that this relationship is positioned as love - especially in situations when the two don't know each other well - is eyebrow-raising. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />3. What is the writing like? Well, the first few pages switch awkwardly between past and present tense, but after that the writing is very good. The tone is moody and atmospheric, and the first part excellently conveys a sense of building dread. But once the direction of the book is revealed at the end of the first part, some of that dread dissipates.<br /><br />4. Are there any loose ends that don't seem to have a place in the story? There are some poorly integrated elements, most notably the dragon orchids. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[They're presented as flowers that a) make people on the island live forever, b) make people on the island infertile, c) have healing powers, and d) can <i>also</i> be brewed into a tea that causes forgetfulness. Then there are the apples which are mentioned once and never again, and apparently those cause happiness. I honestly don't understand what they bring to the story. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />5. Here's some subjectivity for you (if you think everything until this point was subjective, too, I completely agree with you; I think responses to books are all subjective): I liked the explanation of the name Blessed Island. I thought that was well done. <br /><br />Ultimately, <i>Midwinterblood</i> reminded me of <i>Romeo and Juliet</i> and <i>The Lottery</i> with a dash of <i>The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe,</i> minus all plot and with poorly drawn characters whose sole identifying characteristics are relationships through seven generations. I have no idea why it won the Printz, which is about par for the course for me over the past few years.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3566140810632558573" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer891173940" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14533285124183934136">I read this for a book club, and the other book club attendees <i>loved it</i>. They loved it because it was new and different and fresh, because it compelled you to continue reading because you just <i>had to know</i> what was going on, and because it was beautifully written.<br/><br/>I concede all of the above points. It is new and different and fresh, it's beautifully written, and this isn't a book you can really bring yourself to DNF. But when I reached the end, my reaction was, "Huh. Well, that was...weird." I spe</span>
  <span id="freeText14533285124183934136" style="display:none">I read this for a book club, and the other book club attendees <i>loved it</i>. They loved it because it was new and different and fresh, because it compelled you to continue reading because you just <i>had to know</i> what was going on, and because it was beautifully written.<br /><br />I concede all of the above points. It is new and different and fresh, it's beautifully written, and this isn't a book you can really bring yourself to DNF. But when I reached the end, my reaction was, "Huh. Well, that was...weird." I spent the day leading up to my book club discussion trying to figure out if I thought it was good-weird or bad-weird, but in the end, it was just...weird. I didn't like it, but I didn't really <i>dislike</i> it either. I just find it kind of bafflingly odd.<br /><br />If you like weird, you might love this. This book is weird from top to bottom, inside and out. It's got a weird structure, weird characters, weird interconnected stories, and a weird blend of myth and reality. The book is divided into seven parts, and each part is weird in its own unique way.<br /><br />This isn't something I would have picked up without the book club impetus, and this is one of those times when I really could have lived without that extra push. I don't feel like precious hours of my life were wasted with this one, but I don't feel like they were really put to good use either.<br /><br />In sum: Just really strange, leaving me with feelings of ambivalence.<br /><br />P.S. I also have no idea why this is marketed as YA, other than the length and the fact that Marcus Sedgwick had previously published in that genre. It's really not YA in theme, tone, or the age of its central characters, so, uh, what else is there?</span>
  <a data-text-id="14533285124183934136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/550033542?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monica Edinger" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monica Edinger" href="/user/show/221952-monica-edinger">Monica Edinger</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781596438002" href="/book/show/15792870-midwinterblood">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer550033542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10289988643478339584">From <a href='http://medinger.wordpress.com/2013/03/04/marcus-sedgwicks-midwinterblood/' rel='nofollow noopener'>this blog review</a>:<br/><br/>I’m a far-ranging reader, happily reading a picture book one minute and a book for adults the next. Professionally, being a 4th grade teacher and reviewer, not a librarian, I tend to read only YA that really intrigues me for one reason or another and I have to shamefully admit that until now what I’d heard about Marcus Sedgwick’s books — that they were dark and creepy — did not make me want to read them. But recently, I saw something interesting about his latest, <i>Midwinterb</i></span>
  <span id="freeText10289988643478339584" style="display:none">From <a href="http://medinger.wordpress.com/2013/03/04/marcus-sedgwicks-midwinterblood/" rel="nofollow noopener">this blog review</a>:<br /><br />I’m a far-ranging reader, happily reading a picture book one minute and a book for adults the next. Professionally, being a 4th grade teacher and reviewer, not a librarian, I tend to read only YA that really intrigues me for one reason or another and I have to shamefully admit that until now what I’d heard about Marcus Sedgwick’s books — that they were dark and creepy — did not make me want to read them. But recently, I saw something interesting about his latest, <i>Midwinterblood</i>, just as a copy showed up in the mail and so I took it home to read.<br /><br />Wow.<br /><br />The book has an unconventional structure that someone told me is like <i>Cloud Atlas</i>, but while it does have a sort of similar time sense, I’d say it is otherwise completely different. Beginning in 2073 on the island of Blessed, it moves back in time, with an epilogue connecting back to the book’s start. There are seven stories in total, all set on the island, heading back and back and back through time. And by way of these distinctive narratives we are startled to encounter characters we have already met in the earlier stories, characters who care, hate, most of all, two who love throughout eternity. Separately these are ghost stories, love stories, and even something that might be termed dystopic. Playing on tropes of folklore, horror, myth, historical fiction, fantasy, and science fiction, Sedgwick imaginatively weaves something highly original and completely compelling. While Midwinterblood is its own distinct thing, mulling it over now, I think of Laini Taylor’s <i>Lips Touch Three Times</i> and the stories of Margo Lanagan.<br /><br />Most of all, it is gorgeous. Highly recommended.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="10289988643478339584" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_527591849" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/527591849" />
    <a title="Megan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3388215-megan"><img alt="Megan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373331875p2/3388215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/527591849?book_show_action=true">Feb 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan" href="/user/show/3388215-megan">Megan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer527591849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1405596851233426006">I had not heard much about MIDWINTERBLOOD before I picked it up one day on a whim. I had heard good things from a few of my favorite bloggers, and I thought, “Why not?” It’s a story combining the past, the present, and the future, intricately linked in mysterious ways by an island with a very mysterious history. My first reaction was to think of CLOUD ATLAS, but the more I read this story, the more I found myself racing through the pages, I began to realize it was something else entirely.<br/><br/>REINCAR</span>
  <span id="freeText1405596851233426006" style="display:none">I had not heard much about MIDWINTERBLOOD before I picked it up one day on a whim. I had heard good things from a few of my favorite bloggers, and I thought, “Why not?” It’s a story combining the past, the present, and the future, intricately linked in mysterious ways by an island with a very mysterious history. My first reaction was to think of CLOUD ATLAS, but the more I read this story, the more I found myself racing through the pages, I began to realize it was something else entirely.<br /><br />REINCARNATION THROUGH SEVEN CYCLES<br /><br />MIDWINTERBLOOD is not a story like any that is told in young adult fiction often. In fact, in a sense, it isn’t truly just young adult fiction – it is young adult, it is middle grades, it is adult. It has a crossover appeal that will draw in older teens and adults instantly with its variety of characters ranging from archaeologists to journalists to children. On top of this, MIDWINTERBLOOD is a story that begins with the end. And it ends with the end. But the way that Sedgwick intricately entwines the threads of plot was something that immediately called to me.<br /><br />The story is complex, revolving around characters known mostly through the years as Eric and Merle – a changing cast of ages, times, and once gender (sort of) that all comes back to the fact that Erik and Merle are the spirits of two people wrapped in an ancient love, tied to Blessed Island. <br /><br />CREEPY, CHILLING<br /><br />It might not be a traditional horror movie of axe-wielding psychopaths, but at its core, MIDWINTERBLOOD is a story of, well, blood. It’s very bloody, based on the back of an event many centuries ago that resulted in bloodshed. In fact, the seven stories inside its pages revolve around death and include monsters, myths, witches, ghosts, and bombs. Creepy kids are also another major player here.<br /><br />Once I got about 50 pages into MIDWINTERBLOOD, I was hooked and read the rest of the book – it’s rather short, just so you know – in one sitting. I flipped the pages compulsively until I reached the ending and went, “Wow.” It’s a circuitous book that makes sense only if you read the entire book from beginning to end, taking note of every instance of their lives, especially noting the very last vignette and the happenings of the beginning (well, it is the beginning – the beginning is the end is the beginning is the end is a Smashing Pumpkins song with some more endings).<br /><br />But there are issues. One, I was never sure how this was truly a young adult novel. Most of the characters we find are adults, with a few exceptions. Even our main characters in various stories are adults. The narration style was another hang up for me. The way the story was told was somewhat odd and different, and not something I ever truly meshed it. It was always noticeable, especially in the one vignette that was told in first person (maybe it was noticeable because it was the only time the present-tense style ever seemed to fit). But other than this, the story was amazing and almost perfect.<br /><br />VERDICT: An unexpected book, but not without a few issues, MIDWINTERBLOOD is a chilling but enthralling story that pulls you in with ghosts, vampires, and murder, and refuses to let you go until you realize that every word makes sense in the great scheme of things. Definitely check this one out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1405596851233426006" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_155750862" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/155750862" />
    <a title="Kirsty " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3868340-kirsty"><img alt="Kirsty " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1347824234p2/3868340.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/155750862?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kirsty " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kirsty " href="/user/show/3868340-kirsty">Kirsty </a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3868340-kirsty?shelf=ukya">ukya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3868340-kirsty?shelf=review-books">review-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer155750862" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11010632210070278113">Midwinterblood is everything I have come to expect from a Marcus Sedgwick book. It's creepy, clever and keeps with you long after you finish reading it. Oh and you need to read every page before the whole thing finally clicks into place and fully makes sense.<br/><br/>The book is told in sections, each section going back in time from the one before it. I found this way of story telling to be really unusual and a clever way of telling a story. Getting the little snippets throughout time meant you started t</span>
  <span id="freeText11010632210070278113" style="display:none">Midwinterblood is everything I have come to expect from a Marcus Sedgwick book. It's creepy, clever and keeps with you long after you finish reading it. Oh and you need to read every page before the whole thing finally clicks into place and fully makes sense.<br /><br />The book is told in sections, each section going back in time from the one before it. I found this way of story telling to be really unusual and a clever way of telling a story. Getting the little snippets throughout time meant you started to get an overview and started to see a pattern of the story as a whole. <br /><br />There is a main story that runs through the whole book which you start to find more and more out about as the story unfolds itself as you delve deeper into the history of the downright sinister island where it is set. <br /><br />It's hard to say exactly what this book is about without giving too much away about the plotline. Needless to say the story itself twists in turns in way I never saw coming and the storyline is so interesting that it kept me reading page after page. It plays with the ideas of past lives and what a person is willing to sacrifice for someone they love.<br /><br />Another awesome offering which emcompasses everything I have come to expect from a Marcus Sedgwick and well worth a look.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_225210193" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/225210193" />
    <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers"><img alt="TheBookSmugglers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316717753p2/1223249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/225210193?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TheBookSmugglers" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers">TheBookSmugglers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer225210193" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11631674859574569239">Original review posted on <a href='http://thebooksmugglers.com/2011/10/halloween-week-joint-review-midwinterblood-by-marcus-sedgwick.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Book Smugglers</a><br/><br/>Thea’s Take:<br/><br/>I have heard good things about Marcus Sedgwick, so when we were offered the chance to review Midwinterblood, I jumped at the chance. I wasn’t sure what to expect with Midwinterblood, but I certainly had no idea that I would love this book so much. Beautifully composed in seven parts, traveling backwards in time to the origin of Eric and Merle’s tragic story, Midwinterblood is a reverse-palimpsest of sorts – wholly unexpected, haunting, and </span>
  <span id="freeText11631674859574569239" style="display:none">Original review posted on <a href="http://thebooksmugglers.com/2011/10/halloween-week-joint-review-midwinterblood-by-marcus-sedgwick.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Smugglers</a><br /><br />Thea’s Take:<br /><br />I have heard good things about Marcus Sedgwick, so when we were offered the chance to review Midwinterblood, I jumped at the chance. I wasn’t sure what to expect with Midwinterblood, but I certainly had no idea that I would love this book so much. Beautifully composed in seven parts, traveling backwards in time to the origin of Eric and Merle’s tragic story, Midwinterblood is a reverse-palimpsest of sorts – wholly unexpected, haunting, and utterly memorable. I loved it.<br /><br />It’s hard to write this review without spoiling any twists, but I can speak in generalities about how well planned and executed this novel is. Midwinterblood is like a set of matryoshka dolls; each story has another story locked within it, as some detail or memory of an earlier life. The novel in its entirety is the story of two lovers, each born again in seven different incarnations on the same small island, struggling to find each other and achieve some kind of happiness together across the centuries. How exactly their stories play out and why they are chasing each other across different lives, of course, is the true heart of the book and I won’t spoil that for you.<br /><br />I will, however, say that I loved that Eric and Merle’s love is reborn in different ways. They are not always born as lovers – once they are siblings, once they are mother and son, and so on – but they always find a way to be with each other, somehow. It is this twist that made the novel so much more poignant for me as a reader – because doomed love over the ages is a familiar enough theme. Reincarnation as love in all of its forms is something wholly different. Of all the stories, I will say that my favorites are that of the doomed fishmonger and the merchant’s daughter and the brother and sister that must evade an undead threat.<br /><br />Finally, I should mention how perfectly eerie and fitting the setting of Blessed Island is, with its hidden population, its mysterious hidden side, and its dragon-like flower that holds the secret to youth and life. When we are first introduced to the island in the year 2073, and its peculiar, childless inhabitants with secrets to protect, it’s all very Wicker Man-ish.2 I wished that there was more of a uniting thread that would tie Blessed Island and its uniquely potent orchid as well as the conceit of the different types of moons to the story of Eric and Merle, but other than that, Midwinterblood is pretty near perfect. Absolutely recommended, and I’ll definitely be around to read more from Marcus Sedgwick in the near future.<br /><br />Ana’s Take:<br /><br />Having read and enjoyed Marcus Sedgwick’s White Crow, I was very keen to read Midwinterblood. I was expecting a solid, spooky Halloween read but got so much more than that. The book surprised and delighted me with each of its interconnecting stories.<br />It is a story divided in seven parts and it’s about love and sacrifice. It starts at the end – when Eric and Merle meet and fall in love at first sight. Except, it is not the first time they meet and even though the story starts in the future (in 2073), the root of it all lies in the very distant past – and each subsequent story goes back a bit in time going back to when it all started. 3<br /><br />The brilliance of this book is manifold.<br /><br />Part of it comes from the structure itself, divided in small chapters, each story set in a different era as they go back in time. Although the setting – a small, mysterious island – is the same throughout and so are the set of the protagonists (well, sort of), each story reads different from one another – they could be entirely independent had it not been for the ever-present feeling that they are not. Then there is the fact that each story has at least one a very unique distinctive element and most of them are even written in different genres: there is a War Drama, and classic Horror and even a terribly sad Ghost story.<br /><br />Then, there is the fact that this is a love story that acknowledges many different types of love and this is what moved the book from simply good to awesome for me. There is love between mother and son, between siblings, between friends and yes,of course romantic love which also included love between two people of the same gender.<br /><br />My absolute favourite was the aforementioned Ghost story because of not only the story itself but because the author managed to include a story-within-a-story-within-a-story with a twist. Genius.<br /><br />Midwinterblood is a very short book, a quick read (seriously, I devoured it within 2 hours) but one that packs quite the punch. From the beginning it brims with tension and one can’t help but to be engulfed by a suffocating sense of Impending Doom (making it a perfect Halloween read) but more than that, it is a story with heart and it’s full of sadness and sweetness and beauty. I loved it. <br /><br />Rating:<br /><br />Ana: 8 – Excellent<br /><br />Thea: 8 – Excellent</span>
  <a data-text-id="11631674859574569239" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Taylor" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52489703-taylor"><img alt="Taylor" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1542815566p2/52489703.jpg" /></a>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52489703-taylor?shelf=2018-books">2018-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52489703-taylor?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,
